					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-subjectpageheader">
</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Chaotic model of atmospheric convection</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about equations with chaotic solutions. For economics, see <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_curve" title="Lorenz curve">Lorenz curve</a>. For physics, see <a href="/wiki/Lorentz_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Lorentz distribution">Lorentz distribution</a>.</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1305433154">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+link+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+style+.ambox,.mw-parser-output .ambox+.mw-empty-elt+link+link+.ambox{margin-top:-1px}html body.mediawiki .mw-parser-output .ambox.mbox-small-left{margin:4px 1em 4px 0;overflow:hidden;width:238px;border-collapse:collapse;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em}.mw-parser-output .ambox-speedy{border-left:10px solid #b32424;background-color:#fee7e6}.mw-parser-output .ambox-delete{border-left:10px solid #b32424}.mw-parser-output .ambox-content{border-left:10px solid #f28500}.mw-parser-output .ambox-style{border-left:10px solid #fc3}.mw-parser-output .ambox-move{border-left:10px solid #9932cc}.mw-parser-output .ambox-protection{border-left:10px solid #a2a9b1}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-text{border:none;padding:0.25em 0.5em;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image{border:none;padding:2px 0 2px 0.5em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-imageright{border:none;padding:2px 0.5em 2px 0;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-empty-cell{border:none;padding:0;width:1px}.mw-parser-output .ambox .mbox-image-div{width:52px}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .ambox{display:none!important}}</style><table class="box-Technical plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-technical" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/120px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></span></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>may be too technical for most readers to understand</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit">help improve it</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Make_technical_articles_understandable" title="Wikipedia:Make technical articles understandable">make it understandable to non-experts</a>, without removing the technical details.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2023</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Frame"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Trajectory_Through_Phase_Space_in_a_Lorenz_Attractor.gif" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/A_Trajectory_Through_Phase_Space_in_a_Lorenz_Attractor.gif" decoding="async" width="200" height="200" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="200" /></a><figcaption>A sample solution in the Lorenz attractor when <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i>&#160;=&#160;28</span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>σ</i>&#160;=&#160;10</span>, and <span class="texhtml"><i>β</i>&#160;=&#160;<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1214402035">.mw-parser-output .sfrac{white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output .sfrac.tion,.mw-parser-output .sfrac .tion{display:inline-block;vertical-align:-0.5em;font-size:85%;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .num{display:block;line-height:1em;margin:0.0em 0.1em;border-bottom:1px solid}.mw-parser-output .sfrac .den{display:block;line-height:1em;margin:0.1em 0.1em}.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);clip-path:polygon(0px 0px,0px 0px,0px 0px);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px}</style><span class="sfrac">&#8288;<span class="tion"><span class="num">8</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den">3</span></span>&#8288;</span></span></figcaption></figure>
<p>The <b>Lorenz system</b> is a set of three <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_differential_equation" title="Ordinary differential equation">ordinary differential equations</a>, first developed by the meteorologist <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton_Lorenz" title="Edward Norton Lorenz">Edward Lorenz</a> while studying <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">atmospheric convection</a>. It is a classic example of a system that can exhibit <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory" title="Chaos theory">chaotic</a> behavior, meaning its output can be highly sensitive to small changes in its starting conditions.
</p><p>For certain values of its parameters, the system's solutions form a complex, looping pattern known as the <b>Lorenz attractor</b>. The shape of this <a href="/wiki/Attractor" title="Attractor">attractor</a>, when graphed, is famously said to resemble a butterfly. The system's extreme sensitivity to initial conditions gave rise to the popular concept of the <a href="/wiki/Butterfly_effect" title="Butterfly effect">butterfly effect</a>—the idea that a small event, like the flap of a butterfly's wings, could ultimately alter large-scale weather patterns. While the system is <a href="/wiki/Determinism" title="Determinism">deterministic</a>—its future behavior is fully determined by its initial conditions—its chaotic nature makes long-term prediction practically impossible.
</p><p>The behavior of the system depends on the choice of parameters. For some ranges of parameters, the system is predictable: trajectories settle into fixed points or simple periodic orbits, making the long-term behavior easy to describe. For example, when <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> &lt; 1</span>, all solutions converge to the origin, and for certain moderate values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ρ</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">σ</span>, and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">β</span>, solutions converge to symmetric steady states.
</p><p>In contrast, for other parameter ranges, the system becomes chaotic. With the well-known parameters <span class="texhtml"><i>σ</i> = 10</span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> = 28</span>, and <span class="texhtml"><i>β</i> = <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1214402035" /><span class="sfrac">&#8288;<span class="tion"><span class="num">8</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den">3</span></span>&#8288;</span></span>, the solutions never settle down but instead trace out the butterfly-shaped Lorenz attractor. In this regime, small differences in initial conditions grow exponentially. 
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Overview">Overview</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chaos_theory#Lorenz&#39;s_pioneering_contributions_to_chaotic_modeling" title="Chaos theory">Chaos theory §&#160;Lorenz's pioneering contributions to chaotic modeling</a></div>
<p>In 1963, Edward Lorenz developed the system as a simplified mathematical model for <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">atmospheric convection</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lorenz&#95;1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lorenz-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He was attempting to model the way air moves when heated from below and cooled from above. The model describes how three key properties of this system change over time:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is proportional to the intensity of the convection (the rate of fluid flow).</li>
<li><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">y</span> is proportional to the temperature difference between the rising and falling air currents.</li>
<li><span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> is proportional to the distortion of the vertical temperature profile from a linear one.</li></ul>
<p>The model was developed with the assistance of <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Fetter" title="Ellen Fetter">Ellen Fetter</a>, who performed the numerical simulations and created the figures,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lorenz&#95;1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lorenz-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Hamilton_(software_engineer)" title="Margaret Hamilton (software engineer)">Margaret Hamilton</a>, who aided in the initial computations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The behavior of these three variables is governed by the following equations whose values change over time, which is defined as t:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\frac {\mathrm {d} x}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=\sigma (y-x),\\[6pt]{\frac {\mathrm {d} y}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=x(\rho -z)-y,\\[6pt]{\frac {\mathrm {d} z}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=xy-\beta z.\end{aligned}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\frac {\mathrm {d} x}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=\sigma (y-x),\\[6pt]{\frac {\mathrm {d} y}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=x(\rho -z)-y,\\[6pt]{\frac {\mathrm {d} z}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=xy-\beta z.\end{aligned}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7928004d58943529a7be774575a62ca436a82a7f" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -9.171ex; width:20.22ex; height:19.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\frac {\mathrm {d} x}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=\sigma (y-x),\\[6pt]{\frac {\mathrm {d} y}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=x(\rho -z)-y,\\[6pt]{\frac {\mathrm {d} z}{\mathrm {d} t}}&amp;=xy-\beta z.\end{aligned}}}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>The constants <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">σ</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ρ</span>, and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">β</span> are parameters representing physical properties of the system: <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">σ</span> is the <a href="/wiki/Prandtl_number" title="Prandtl number">Prandtl number</a>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ρ</span> is the <a href="/wiki/Rayleigh_number" title="Rayleigh number">Rayleigh number</a>, and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">β</span> relates to the physical dimensions of the fluid layer itself.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sparrow&#95;1982&#95;3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sparrow_1982-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>From a technical standpoint, the Lorenz system is <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_system" title="Nonlinear system">nonlinear</a>, aperiodic, three-dimensional, and <a href="/wiki/Deterministic_system_(mathematics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Deterministic system (mathematics)">deterministic</a>. While originally for weather, the equations have since been found to model behavior in a wide variety of systems, including <a href="/wiki/Laser" title="Laser">lasers</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electric_generator" title="Electric generator">dynamos</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electrical_network" title="Electrical network">electric circuits</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and even some <a href="/wiki/Chemical_reaction" title="Chemical reaction">chemical reactions</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Lorenz equations have been the subject of hundreds of research articles and at least one book-length study.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Sparrow&#95;1982&#95;3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sparrow_1982-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Analysis">Analysis</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Analysis"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>One normally assumes that the parameters <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">σ</span>, <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ρ</span>, and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">β</span> are positive. Lorenz used the values <span class="texhtml"><i>σ</i> = 10</span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> = 28</span>, and <span class="texhtml"><i>β</i> = <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1214402035" /><span class="sfrac">&#8288;<span class="tion"><span class="num">8</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den">3</span></span>&#8288;</span></span>. The system exhibits chaotic behavior for these (and nearby) values.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>If <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> &lt; 1</span> then there is only one <a href="/wiki/Equilibrium_point_(mathematics)" title="Equilibrium point (mathematics)">equilibrium point</a>, which is at the origin. This point corresponds to no convection. All <a href="/wiki/Orbit_(dynamics)" title="Orbit (dynamics)">orbits</a> converge to the origin, which is a global <a href="/wiki/Attractor" title="Attractor">attractor</a>, when <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> &lt; 1</span>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_bifurcation" title="Pitchfork bifurcation">pitchfork bifurcation</a> occurs at <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> = 1</span>, and for <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> &gt; 1</span> two additional equilibrium points appear at
<span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-block"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-display mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math display="block" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \left({\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},\rho -1\right)\quad {\text{and}}\quad \left(-{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},-{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},\rho -1\right).}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow>
          <mo>(</mo>
          <mrow>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <msqrt>
                <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>

                <mn>1</mn>
                <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
              </msqrt>
            </mrow>
            <mo>,</mo>

          </mrow>
          <mo>)</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mspace width="1em" />
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mtext>and</mtext>
        </mrow>
        <mspace width="1em" />
        <mrow>
          <mo>(</mo>
          <mrow>
            <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <msqrt>
                <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                <mi>&#x03C1;<!-- ρ --></mi>
                <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
                <mn>1</mn>
                <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
              </msqrt>
            </mrow>
            <mo>,</mo>
            <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <msqrt>
                <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>

                <mi>&#x03C1;<!-- ρ --></mi>
                <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
                <mn>1</mn>
                <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
              </msqrt>
            </mrow>
            <mo>,</mo>
            <mi>&#x03C1;<!-- ρ --></mi>
            <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
            <mn>1</mn>
          </mrow>
          <mo>)</mo>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \left({\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},\rho -1\right)\quad {\text{and}}\quad \left(-{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},-{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},\rho -1\right).}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9dc193f435127809b478b8cb6dfce2015649eff5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-display mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:76.593ex; height:4.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \left({\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},\rho -1\right)\quad {\text{and}}\quad \left(-{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},-{\sqrt {\beta (\rho -1)}},\rho -1\right).}"></span>
These correspond to <a href="/wiki/Steady_state" title="Steady state">steady</a> convection. This pair of equilibrium points is <a href="/wiki/Stability_theory" title="Stability theory">stable</a> only if 
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \rho &lt;\sigma {\frac {\sigma +\beta +3}{\sigma -\beta -1}},}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>&#x03C1;<!-- ρ --></mi>
        <mo>&lt;</mo>
        <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- σ --></mi>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- σ --></mi>
              <mo>+</mo>
              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
              <mo>+</mo>
              <mn>3</mn>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- σ --></mi>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>1</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>,</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \rho &lt;\sigma {\frac {\sigma +\beta +3}{\sigma -\beta -1}},}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/01ccdbc7bc857ba7aceddb06b92d9882ae7e9c0c" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:16.618ex; height:5.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle \rho &lt;\sigma {\frac {\sigma +\beta +3}{\sigma -\beta -1}},}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>which can hold only for positive <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ρ</span> if <span class="texhtml"><i>σ</i> &gt; <i>β</i> + 1</span>. At the critical value, both equilibrium points lose stability through a subcritical <a href="/wiki/Hopf_bifurcation" title="Hopf bifurcation">Hopf bifurcation</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>When <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i>&#160;=&#160;28</span>, <span class="texhtml"><i>σ</i>&#160;=&#160;10</span>, and <span class="texhtml"><i>β</i>&#160;=&#160;<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1214402035" /><span class="sfrac">&#8288;<span class="tion"><span class="num">8</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den">3</span></span>&#8288;</span></span>, the Lorenz system has <a href="/wiki/Deterministic_chaos" class="mw-redirect" title="Deterministic chaos">chaotic solutions</a> (but not all solutions are chaotic). Almost all initial points will tend to an <a href="/wiki/Invariant_set" class="mw-redirect" title="Invariant set">invariant set</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;the Lorenz attractor&#160;&#8211;&#32;a <a href="/wiki/Attractor#Strange_attractor" title="Attractor">strange attractor</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fractal" title="Fractal">fractal</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Hidden_attractor#Self-excited_attractors" title="Hidden attractor">self-excited attractor</a> with respect to all three equilibria. Its <a href="/wiki/Hausdorff_dimension" title="Hausdorff dimension">Hausdorff dimension</a> is estimated from above by the <a href="/wiki/Lyapunov_dimension" title="Lyapunov dimension">Lyapunov dimension (Kaplan-Yorke dimension)</a> as <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7000206000000000000♠"></span>2.06<span style="margin-left:0.225em;margin-right:0.225em;">±</span>0.01</span>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Kuznetsov-2020-ND&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuznetsov-2020-ND-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Correlation_dimension" title="Correlation dimension">correlation dimension</a> is estimated to be <span class="nowrap"><span data-sort-value="7000204999999999999♠"></span>2.05<span style="margin-left:0.225em;margin-right:0.225em;">±</span>0.01</span>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The exact Lyapunov dimension formula of the global attractor can be found analytically under classical restrictions on the parameters:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Kuznetsov-2020-ND&#95;11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kuznetsov-2020-ND-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-2020-KuznetsovR&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020-KuznetsovR-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle 3-{\frac {2(\sigma +\beta +1)}{\sigma +1+{\sqrt {\left(\sigma -1\right)^{2}+4\sigma \rho }}}}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mn>3</mn>
        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mn>2</mn>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- σ --></mi>
              <mo>+</mo>
              <mi>&#x03B2;<!-- β --></mi>
              <mo>+</mo>
              <mn>1</mn>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- σ --></mi>
              <mo>+</mo>
              <mn>1</mn>
              <mo>+</mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <msqrt>
                  <msup>
                    <mrow>
                      <mo>(</mo>
                      <mrow>
                        <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- σ --></mi>
                        <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
                        <mn>1</mn>
                      </mrow>
                      <mo>)</mo>
                    </mrow>
                    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                      <mn>2</mn>
                    </mrow>
                  </msup>
                  <mo>+</mo>
                  <mn>4</mn>
                  <mi>&#x03C3;<!-- σ --></mi>
                  <mi>&#x03C1;<!-- ρ --></mi>
                </msqrt>
              </mrow>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 3-{\frac {2(\sigma +\beta +1)}{\sigma +1+{\sqrt {\left(\sigma -1\right)^{2}+4\sigma \rho }}}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2e7ef58eb6ef390caa3455447d34510547931d4a" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -4.671ex; width:30.066ex; height:8.509ex;" alt="{\displaystyle 3-{\frac {2(\sigma +\beta +1)}{\sigma +1+{\sqrt {\left(\sigma -1\right)^{2}+4\sigma \rho }}}}}"></span></dd></dl>
<p>The Lorenz attractor is difficult to analyze, but the action of the differential equation on the attractor is described by a fairly simple geometric model.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Proving that this is indeed the case is the fourteenth problem on the list of <a href="/wiki/Smale%27s_problems" title="Smale&#39;s problems">Smale's problems</a>. This problem was the first one to be resolved, by <a href="/wiki/Warwick_Tucker" title="Warwick Tucker">Warwick Tucker</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Tucker&#95;2002&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker_2002-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For other values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ρ</span>, the system displays knotted periodic orbits. For example, with <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> = 99.96</span> it becomes a <span class="texhtml"><i>T</i>(3,2)</span> <a href="/wiki/Torus_knot" title="Torus knot">torus knot</a>.
</p>

</td></tr>
<tr>
<td align="center" colspan="2">For small values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">ρ</span>, the system is stable and evolves to one of two fixed point attractors. When <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> &gt; 24.74</span>, the fixed points become repulsors and the trajectory is repelled by them in a very complex way.

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Connection_to_the_tent_map">Connection to the tent map</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Connection to the tent map"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lorenz_Map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lorenz_Map.png/330px-Lorenz_Map.png" decoding="async" width="330" height="193" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lorenz_Map.png/500px-Lorenz_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Lorenz_Map.png/720px-Lorenz_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="420" /></a><figcaption>A recreation of Lorenz's results created on <a href="/wiki/Mathematica" class="mw-redirect" title="Mathematica">Mathematica</a>. Points above the red line correspond to the system switching lobes.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In Figure 4 of his paper,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-lorenz&#95;1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lorenz-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Lorenz plotted the relative maximum value in the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> direction achieved by the system against the previous relative maximum in the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> direction. This procedure later became known as a Lorenz map (not to be confused with a <a href="/wiki/Poincar%C3%A9_plot" title="Poincaré plot">Poincaré plot</a>, which plots the intersections of a trajectory with a prescribed surface). The resulting plot has a shape very similar to the <a href="/wiki/Tent_map" title="Tent map">tent map</a>. Lorenz also found that when the maximum <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> value is above a certain cut-off, the system will switch to the next lobe. Combining this with the chaos known to be exhibited by the tent map, he showed that the system switches between the two lobes chaotically.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Simulations">Simulations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Simulations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:3D_Lorenz_Chaotic_Attactor.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/3D_Lorenz_Chaotic_Attactor.png/250px-3D_Lorenz_Chaotic_Attactor.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="175" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/3D_Lorenz_Chaotic_Attactor.png/500px-3D_Lorenz_Chaotic_Attactor.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="700" /></a><figcaption>A plot of the 3D simulation</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lorenz_attractor_in_Julia.gif" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Lorenz System simulation in Julia" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Lorenz_attractor_in_Julia.gif/250px-Lorenz_attractor_in_Julia.gif" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Lorenz_attractor_in_Julia.gif/500px-Lorenz_attractor_in_Julia.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a><figcaption>Julia simulation</figcaption></figure>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Maple_simulation"><a href="/wiki/Maple_(software)" title="Maple (software)">Maple</a> simulation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Maple simulation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-mupad mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="nv">deq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">:=</span><span class="w"> </span><span </p>

<span class="n">soln</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="nv">t_</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">StateResponse</span><span class="p">[{</span><span class="n">lorenz</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="mi">10</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">10</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">10</span><span class="p">}},</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="mi">10</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">28</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">8</span><span class="o">/</span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">},</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="n">t</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">50</span><span class="p">}];</span>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="R_simulation"><a href="/wiki/R_(programming_language)" title="R (programming language)">R</a> simulation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: R simulation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-r mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="nf">library</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">deSolve</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="nf">library</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">plotly</span><span class="p">)</span>

<span class="c1"># parameters</span>
<span class="n">prm</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">list</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sigma</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">10</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">rho</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">28</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">beta</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">8</span><span class="o">/</span><span class="m">3</span><span class="p">)</span>

<span class="c1"># initial values</span>
<span class="n">varini</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">c</span><span class="p">(</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="n">X</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">1</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="n">Y</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="n">Z</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">1</span>
<span class="p">)</span>

<span class="n">Lorenz</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">function</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">t</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vars</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">prm</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nf">with</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nf">as.list</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vars</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">dX</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">prm</span><span class="o">$</span><span class="n">sigma</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">Y</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">X</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">dY</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">X</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">prm</span><span class="o">$</span><span class="n">rho</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Z</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Y</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">dZ</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">X</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">Y</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">prm</span><span class="o">$</span><span class="n">beta</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">Z</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="kr">return</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nf">list</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nf">c</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">dX</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">dY</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">dZ</span><span class="p">)))</span>
<span class="w">   </span><span class="p">})</span>
<span class="p">}</span>

<span class="n">times</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">seq</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">from</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">to</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">100</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">by</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">0.01</span><span class="p">)</span>

<span class="c1"># call ODE solver</span>
<span class="n">out</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">ode</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">y</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">varini</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">times</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">times</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">func</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Lorenz</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">           </span><span class="n">parms</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">prm</span><span class="p">)</span>

<span class="c1"># to assign color to points</span>
<span class="n">gfill</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">function</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">repArr</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">long</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="nf">rep</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">repArr</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">ceiling</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">long</span><span class="o">/</span><span class="nf">length</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">repArr</span><span class="p">)))[</span><span class="m">1</span><span class="o">:</span><span class="n">long</span><span class="p">]</span>

<span class="n">dout</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">as.data.frame</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">out</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="n">dout</span><span class="o">$</span><span class="n">color</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&lt;-</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">gfill</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nf">rainbow</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="m">10</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">nrow</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">dout</span><span class="p">))</span>

<span class="c1"># Graphics production with Plotly:</span>
<span class="nf">plot_ly</span><span class="p">(</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="n">data</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="n">dout</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">~</span><span class="n">X</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">y</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">~</span><span class="n">Y</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">z</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">~</span><span class="n">Z</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="n">type</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#39;scatter3d&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">mode</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#39;lines&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span>
<span class="w">  </span><span class="n">opacity</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">line</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">list</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">width</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="m">6</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">color</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">~</span><span class="n">color</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">reverscale</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">FALSE</span><span class="p">)</span>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="SageMath_simulation"><a href="/wiki/SageMath" title="SageMath">SageMath</a> simulation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: SageMath simulation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-r mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="c1"># we solve the Lorenz system of differential equations with initial conditions y_1(0) = 0, y_2(0) = 0.5, y_3(0) = 0.</span>
<span class="c1"># Runge-Kutta&#39;s method y_{n+1}= y_n + h*(k_1 + 2*k_2+2*k_3+k_4)/6; x_{n+1}=x_n+h</span>
<span class="c1"># k_1=f(x_n,y_n), k_2=f(x_n+h/2, y_n+hk_1/2), k_3=f(x_n+h/2, y_n+hk_2/2), k_4=f(x_n+h, y_n+hk_3)</span>
<span class="c1"># differential equation</span>

<span class="n">def</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">Runge_Kutta</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">f</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="n">h</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="n">n</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">tlist</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="o">+</span><span class="n">i</span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">h</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">i</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">n</span><span class="m">+1</span><span class="p">)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">y</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[[</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">for</span><span class="w"> </span>_<span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">n</span><span class="m">+1</span><span class="p">)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="c1"># Taking length of f (number of equations).</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="nf">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">f</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="c1"># Number of variables in v.</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">vm</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="nf">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="kr">if</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="o">!=</span><span class="n">vm</span><span class="o">:</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="kr">return</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&quot;error, number of equations is not equal with the number of variables.&quot;</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="kr">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">r</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vm</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span>
<span class="w">        </span><span class="n">y</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="p">][</span><span class="n">r</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">r</span><span class="p">]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="c1"># making a vector and component will be a list    </span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="c1"># main part of the algorithm    </span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">k1</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">for</span><span class="w"> </span>_<span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">m</span><span class="p">)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">k2</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">for</span><span class="w"> </span>_<span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">m</span><span class="p">)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">k3</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">for</span><span class="w"> </span>_<span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">m</span><span class="p">)]</span>
<span class="w">    </span><span class="n">k4</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="m">0</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">for</span><span class="w"> </span>_<span class="w"> </span><span class="kr">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nf">range</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">m</span><span class="p">)]</span>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Applications">Applications</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Model_for_atmospheric_convection">Model for atmospheric convection</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Model for atmospheric convection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>As shown in Lorenz's original paper,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the Lorenz system is a reduced version of a larger system studied earlier by Barry Saltzman.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Lorenz equations are derived from the <a href="/wiki/Boussinesq_approximation_(buoyancy)" title="Boussinesq approximation (buoyancy)">Oberbeck–Boussinesq approximation</a> to the equations describing fluid circulation in a shallow layer of fluid, heated uniformly from below and cooled uniformly from above.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This fluid circulation is known as <a href="/wiki/Rayleigh%E2%80%93B%C3%A9nard_convection" title="Rayleigh–Bénard convection">Rayleigh–Bénard convection</a>. The fluid is assumed to circulate in two dimensions (vertical and horizontal) with periodic rectangular boundary conditions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The partial differential equations modeling the system's <a href="/wiki/Stream_function" title="Stream function">stream function</a> and temperature are subjected to a spectral <a href="/wiki/Galerkin_method" title="Galerkin method">Galerkin approximation</a>: the hydrodynamic fields are expanded in <a href="/wiki/Fourier_series" title="Fourier series">Fourier series</a>, which are then severely truncated to a single term for the stream function and two terms for the temperature. This reduces the model equations to a set of three coupled, <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_system" title="Nonlinear system">nonlinear</a> ordinary differential equations. A detailed derivation may be found, for example, in nonlinear dynamics texts from <a href="#CITEREFHilborn2000">Hilborn (2000)</a>, Appendix C;  <a href="#CITEREFBergéPomeauVidal1984">Bergé, Pomeau &amp; Vidal (1984)</a>, Appendix D; or Shen (2016),<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Supplementary Materials.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Model_for_the_nature_of_chaos_and_order_in_the_atmosphere">Model for the nature of chaos and order in the atmosphere</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Model for the nature of chaos and order in the atmosphere"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The scientific community accepts that the chaotic features found in low-dimensional Lorenz models could represent features of the Earth's atmosphere,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> yielding the statement of “weather is chaotic.” By comparison, based on the concept of attractor coexistence within the generalized Lorenz model<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the original Lorenz model,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Shen and his co-authors proposed a revised view that “weather possesses both chaos and order with distinct predictability”.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The revised view,&#160;which is a build-up of the conventional view, is used to suggest that “the chaotic and regular features found in theoretical Lorenz models could better represent features of the Earth's atmosphere”.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Resolution_of_Smale's_14th_problem"><span id="Resolution_of_Smale.27s_14th_problem"></span>Resolution of Smale's 14th problem</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lorenz_system&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Resolution of Smale&#039;s 14th problem"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Smale%27s_problems" title="Smale&#39;s problems">Smale's 14th problem</a> asks, "Do the properties of the Lorenz attractor exhibit that of a <a href="/wiki/Attractor#Strange_attractor" title="Attractor">strange attractor</a>?". The problem was answered affirmatively by <a href="/wiki/Warwick_Tucker" title="Warwick Tucker">Warwick Tucker</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Tucker&#95;2002&#95;16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker_2002-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> To prove this result, Tucker used rigorous <a href="/wiki/Numerical_analysis" title="Numerical analysis">numerics methods</a> like <a href="/wiki/Interval_arithmetic" title="Interval arithmetic">interval arithmetic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Normal_form_(dynamical_systems)" title="Normal form (dynamical systems)">normal forms</a>. First, Tucker defined a cross section <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma \subset \{x_{3}=r-1\}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi mathvariant="normal">&#x03A3;<!-- Σ --></mi>
        <mo>&#x2282;<!-- ⊂ --></mo>
        <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">{</mo>
        <msub>
          <mi>x</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mn>3</mn>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mi>r</mi>

        <mn>1</mn>
        <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">}</mo>
      </mstyle>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \Sigma \subset \{x_{3}=r-1\}}</annotation>
  </semantics>

From this, one can define the first-return map <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle P}">

</p><p>Then the proof is split in three main points that are proved and imply the existence of a strange attractor.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Viana&#95;2000&#95;29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Viana_2000-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The three points are:
</p>
<ul><li>There exists a region <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle N\subset \Sigma }">

<li>The return map admits a forward invariant cone field.</li>
<li>Vectors inside this invariant cone field are uniformly expanded by the derivative <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle DP}">

<p>To prove the first point, we notice that the cross section <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma }">

The goal is to do this method recursively until the flow comes back to <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle \Sigma }">

            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P(R_{i})\subset Rf_{i}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1dadf84b0f22f548dc26fcc91403bfec3437ccd8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:12.92ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle P(R_{i})\subset Rf_{i}}"></span>. The problem is that our estimation may become imprecise after several iterations, thus what Tucker does is to split <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle R_{i}'}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msubsup>
          <mi>R</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
          </mrow>
          <mo>&#x2032;</mo>
        </msubsup>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle R_{i}'}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/875659c78c85a3e6252649f4ebaa9a63b0605bdf" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.564ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle R_{i}&#039;}"></span> into smaller rectangles <span class="mwe-math-element mwe-math-element-inline"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"  alttext="{\displaystyle R_{i,j}}">
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <msub>
          <mi>R</mi>
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mi>i</mi>
            <mo>,</mo>
            <mi>j</mi>
          </mrow>
        </msub>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle R_{i,j}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7bb6f9df8716f0eb2d1e8bc277932500b81eb62b" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline mw-invert skin-invert" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.699ex; height:2.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle R_{i,j}}"></span> and then apply the process recursively. Another problem is that as we are applying this algorithm, the flow becomes more 'horizontal',<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Viana&#95;2000&#95;29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Viana_2000-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> leading to a dramatic increase in imprecision. To prevent this, the algorithm changes the orientation of the cross sections, becoming either horizontal or vertical.
</p>

			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Intermittent_Lorenz_Attractor_-_Chaoscope.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="A visualization of the Lorenz attractor near an intermittent cycle."><img alt="A visualization of the Lorenz attractor near an intermittent cycle." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Intermittent_Lorenz_Attractor_-_Chaoscope.jpg/120px-Intermittent_Lorenz_Attractor_-_Chaoscope.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="120" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Intermittent_Lorenz_Attractor_-_Chaoscope.jpg/250px-Intermittent_Lorenz_Attractor_-_Chaoscope.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">A visualization of the Lorenz attractor near an intermittent cycle.</div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lorenz_apparition_small.gif" class="mw-file-description" title="Two streamlines in a Lorenz system, from ρ = 0 to ρ = 28 (σ = 10, β = ⁠8/3⁠)."><img alt="Two streamlines in a Lorenz system, from ρ = 0 to ρ = 28 (σ = 10, β = ⁠8/3⁠)." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lorenz_apparition_small.gif/120px-Lorenz_apparition_small.gif" decoding="async" width="120" height="67" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Lorenz_apparition_small.gif/250px-Lorenz_apparition_small.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="625" data-file-height="351" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">Two streamlines in a Lorenz system, from <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> = 0</span> to <span class="texhtml"><i>ρ</i> = 28</span> <span class="avoidwrap" style="display:inline-block;">(<span class="texhtml"><i>σ</i> = 10</span>,</span> <span class="texhtml"><i>β</i> = <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1214402035" /><span class="sfrac">&#8288;<span class="tion"><span class="num">8</span><span class="sr-only">/</span><span class="den">3</span></span>&#8288;</span></span>).</div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lorenz(rho).gif" class="mw-file-description" title="Animation of a Lorenz System with rho-dependence."><img alt="Animation of a Lorenz System with rho-dependence." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lorenz%28rho%29.gif/120px-Lorenz%28rho%29.gif" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lorenz%28rho%29.gif/250px-Lorenz%28rho%29.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></span></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">Animation of a Lorenz System with rho-dependence.</div>
		</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px; height: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Lorenz_Attractor_Brain_Dynamics_Toolbox.gif" class="mw-file-description" title="Animation of the Lorenz attractor in the Brain Dynamics Toolbox.[30]"><img alt="Animation of the Lorenz attractor in the Brain Dynamics Toolbox.[30]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Lorenz_Attractor_Brain_Dynamics_Toolbox.gif/120px-Lorenz_Attractor_Brain_Dynamics_Toolbox.gif" decoding="async" width="120" height="90" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Lorenz_Attractor_Brain_Dynamics_Toolbox.gif/250px-Lorenz_Attractor_Brain_Dynamics_Toolbox.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="400" /></a></span></div>

		</li>

(2022). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mdpi.com/2227-7390/10/8/1207/pdf">"On a high-precision method for studying attractors of dynamical systems and systems of explosive type"</a>. <i>Mathematics</i>. <b>10</b> (8): 1207. <a href="/wiki/ArXiv_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ArXiv (identifier)">arXiv</a>:<span class="id-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://arxiv.org/abs/2206.08195">2206.08195</a></span>. <a href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<span class="id-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.3390%2Fmath10081207">10.3390/math10081207</a></span>.</cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Mathematics&amp;rft.atitle=On+a+high-precision+method+for+studying+attractors+of+dynamical+systems+and+systems+of+explosive+type&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=8&amp;rft.pages=1207&amp;rft.date=2022&amp;rft&#95;id=info%3Aarxiv%2F2206.08195&amp;rft&#95;id=info%3Adoi%2F10.3390%2Fmath10081207&amp;rft.aulast=Pchelintsev&amp;rft.aufirst=A.N.&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.mdpi.com%2F2227-7390%2F10%2F8%2F1207%2Fpdf&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALorenz+system" class="Z3988"></span></li></ul>
